      <p>The <b>Central African Republic</b> (<b>CAR</b>; <a href="/wiki/Sango_language" title="Sango language">Sango</a>: <i>KÃ¶dÃ¶rÃ¶sÃªse tÃ® BÃªafrÃ®ka</i><span style="margin-left:1px">;</span> <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>: <i lang="fr">RÃ©publique centrafricaine</i> (<b>RCA</b><sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup>), <small>French:&nbsp;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/French" title="Help:IPA/French">[Êepyblik sÉÌtÊafÊikÉn]</a></span>, or <i><i lang="fr" title="French-language text">Centrafrique</i></i> <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/French" title="Help:IPA/French">[sÉÌtÊafÊik]</a></span>) is a <a href="/wiki/Landlocked_country" title="Landlocked country">landlocked country</a> in <a href="/wiki/Central_Africa" title="Central Africa">Central Africa</a>. It is bordered by <a href="/wiki/Chad" title="Chad">Chad</a> to <a href="/wiki/Central_African_Republic%E2%80%93Chad_border" title="Central African RepublicâChad border">the north</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sudan" title="Sudan">Sudan</a> to <a href="/wiki/Central_African_Republic%E2%80%93Sudan_border" title="Central African RepublicâSudan border">the northeast</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Sudan" title="South Sudan">South Sudan</a> to <a href="/wiki/Central_African_Republic%E2%80%93South_Sudan_border" title="Central African RepublicâSouth Sudan border">the southeast</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Democratic Republic of the Congo">Democratic Republic of the Congo</a> to <a href="/wiki/Central_African_Republic%E2%80%93Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo_border" title="Central African RepublicâDemocratic Republic of the Congo border">the south</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Republic of the Congo">Republic of the Congo</a> to <a href="/wiki/Central_African_Republic%E2%80%93Republic_of_the_Congo_border" title="Central African RepublicâRepublic of the Congo border">the southwest</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cameroon" title="Cameroon">Cameroon</a> to <a href="/wiki/Cameroon%E2%80%93Central_African_Republic_border" title="CameroonâCentral African Republic border">the west</a>. The CAR covers a land area of about 620,000 square kilometres (240,000&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi) and had an estimated population of around 4.7 million as of 2018<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Central_African_Republic&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>. As of 2021<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Central_African_Republic&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the CAR is the scene of a <a href="/wiki/Central_African_Republic_Civil_War" title="Central African Republic Civil War">civil war, ongoing since 2012</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Most of the CAR consists of Sudano-Guinean <a href="/wiki/Savanna" title="Savanna">savannas</a>, but the country also includes a <a href="/wiki/Sahel" title="Sahel">Sahelo</a>-<a href="/wiki/East_Sudanian_savanna" title="East Sudanian savanna">Sudanian</a> zone in the north and an <a href="/wiki/Northern_Congolian_forest-savanna_mosaic" class="mw-redirect" title="Northern Congolian forest-savanna mosaic">equatorial forest zone</a> in the south. Two-thirds of the country is within the <a href="/wiki/Ubangi_River" title="Ubangi River">Ubangi River</a> basin (which flows into the <a href="/wiki/Congo_River" title="Congo River">Congo</a>), while the remaining third lies in the basin of the <a href="/wiki/Chari_River" title="Chari River">Chari</a>, which flows into <a href="/wiki/Lake_Chad" title="Lake Chad">Lake Chad</a>. </p>
      <p>What is today the Central African Republic has been inhabited for millennia; however, the country's current borders were established by <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>, which ruled the country as a colony starting in the late 19th century. After gaining independence from France in 1960, the Central African Republic was ruled by a series of autocratic leaders, including an <a href="/wiki/Central_African_Empire" title="Central African Empire">abortive attempt at a monarchy</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-Bokassa_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bokassa-11">[11]</a></sup> by the 1990s, calls for democracy led to the first multi-party democratic elections in 1993. <a href="/wiki/Ange-F%C3%A9lix_Patass%C3%A9" title="Ange-FÃ©lix PatassÃ©">Ange-FÃ©lix PatassÃ©</a> became president, but was later removed by <a href="/wiki/Fran%C3%A7ois_Boziz%C3%A9" title="FranÃ§ois BozizÃ©">General FranÃ§ois BozizÃ©</a> in the <a href="/wiki/2003_Central_African_Republic_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="2003 Central African Republic coup d'Ã©tat">2003 coup</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Central_African_Republic_Bush_War" title="Central African Republic Bush War">Central African Republic Bush War</a> began in 2004 and, despite a peace treaty in 2007 and another in 2011, civil war resumed in 2012, perpetuating the country's poor <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_the_Central_African_Republic" title="Human rights in the Central African Republic">human rights record</a>, characterized by widespread and increasing abuses by various participating armed groups, such as arbitrary imprisonment, torture and restrictions on freedom of the press and freedom of movement. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Resource_curse" title="Resource curse">Despite</a> its significant <a href="/wiki/Mineral" title="Mineral">mineral</a> deposits and other resources, such as <a href="/wiki/Uranium" title="Uranium">uranium</a> reserves, <a href="/wiki/Crude_oil" class="mw-redirect" title="Crude oil">crude oil</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gold" title="Gold">gold</a>, <a href="/wiki/Diamond" title="Diamond">diamonds</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cobalt" title="Cobalt">cobalt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lumber" title="Lumber">lumber</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Hydropower" title="Hydropower">hydropower</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-12">[12]</a></sup> as well as significant quantities of <a href="/wiki/Arable_land" title="Arable land">arable land</a>, the Central African Republic is among the ten poorest countries in the world, with the lowest <a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">GDP</a> per capita at purchasing power parity in the world as of 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-IMF_2017_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IMF_2017-13">[13]</a></sup> As of 2019<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Central_African_Republic&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, according to the <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Index" title="Human Development Index">Human Development Index</a> (HDI), the country had the second-lowest level of human development (only behind <a href="/wiki/Niger" title="Niger">Niger</a>), ranking 188th out of 189 countries, and the country had the lowest <a href="/wiki/Inequality-adjusted_Human_Development_Index" class="mw-redirect" title="Inequality-adjusted Human Development Index">inequality-adjusted Human Development Index</a> (IHDI), ranking 150th out of 150 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-HDI_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HDI-14">[14]</a></sup> It is also estimated to be the unhealthiest country<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> as well as the worst country in which to be young.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> The Central African Republic is a member of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>, the <a href="/wiki/African_Union" title="African Union">African Union</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Economic_Community_of_Central_African_States" title="Economic Community of Central African States">Economic Community of Central African States</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Organisation_internationale_de_la_Francophonie" title="Organisation internationale de la Francophonie">Organisation internationale de la Francophonie</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Non-Aligned_Movement" title="Non-Aligned Movement">Non-Aligned Movement</a>. </p>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Central_African_Republic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>The name of the Central African Republic is derived from the country's geographical location in the central region of Africa and its republic form of government. From 1976 to 1979, the country was known as the Central African Empire. During the colonial era, the country's name was Ubangi-Shari which is derived from the <a href="/wiki/Ubangi_River" title="Ubangi River">Ubangi River</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Chari_River" title="Chari River">Chari River</a>. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Central_African_Republic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Central_African_Republic" title="History of the Central African Republic">History of the Central African Republic</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Bouar_Megaliths_stamp.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Bouar_Megaliths_stamp.jpg/170px-Bouar_Megaliths_stamp.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="259" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/8/80/Bouar_Megaliths_stamp.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="197" data-file-height="300"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Bouar_Megaliths_stamp.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/Bouar" title="Bouar">Bouar</a> Megaliths, pictured here on a 1967 Central African stamp, date back to the very late Neolithic Era (c. 3500â2700 BC).
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_history">Early history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Central_African_Republic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Early history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Approximately 10,000 years ago, <a href="/wiki/Desertification" title="Desertification">desertification</a> forced hunter-gatherer societies south into the Sahel regions of northern Central Africa, where some groups settled.<sup id="cite_ref-Eastern_Africa_2011,_pg._4_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eastern_Africa_2011,_pg._4-17">[17]</a></sup> Farming began as part of the <a href="/wiki/Neolithic_Revolution" title="Neolithic Revolution">Neolithic Revolution</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> Initial farming of <a href="/wiki/Dioscorea_rotundata" class="mw-redirect" title="Dioscorea rotundata">white yam</a> progressed into <a href="/wiki/Millet" title="Millet">millet</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sorghum" title="Sorghum">sorghum</a>, and before 3000 BC<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> the domestication of <a href="/wiki/Elaeis_guineensis" title="Elaeis guineensis">African oil palm</a> improved the groups' nutrition and allowed for expansion of the local populations.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> This Agricultural Revolution, combined with a "Fish-stew Revolution", in which fishing began to take place, and the use of boats, allowed for the transportation of goods. Products were often moved in <a href="/wiki/Ceramic" title="Ceramic">ceramic</a> pots, which are the first known examples of <a href="/wiki/Artistic_expression" class="mw-redirect" title="Artistic expression">artistic expression</a> from the region's inhabitants. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Bouar" title="Bouar">Bouar Megaliths</a> in the western region of the country indicate an advanced level of habitation dating back to the very late <a href="/wiki/Neolithic" title="Neolithic">Neolithic Era</a> (c. 3500â2700 BC).<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ferrous_metallurgy" title="Ferrous metallurgy">Ironworking</a> arrived in the region around 1000 BC. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Azande_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Azande people">Azande people</a> settled along the <a href="/wiki/Ubangi_River" title="Ubangi River">Ubangi River</a> in what is today Central and East CAR, while <a href="/wiki/Bantoid" class="mw-redirect" title="Bantoid">Bantoid</a> peoples migrated from the southwest from Cameroon.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Banana" title="Banana">Bananas</a> arrived in the region during the first millennium BCE<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> and added an important source of carbohydrates to the diet; they were also used in the production of <a href="/wiki/Alcoholic_beverages" class="mw-redirect" title="Alcoholic beverages">alcoholic beverages</a>. Production of <a href="/wiki/Copper" title="Copper">copper</a>, <a href="/wiki/Salt" title="Salt">salt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dried_fish" title="Dried fish">dried fish</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Textiles" class="mw-redirect" title="Textiles">textiles</a> dominated the economic trade in the Central African region.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span id="16th.E2.80.9319th_century"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="16thâ19th_century">16thâ19th century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Central_African_Republic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 16thâ19th century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Sultan_and_his_wives_at_Bangassou,_1906.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Sultan_and_his_wives_at_Bangassou%2C_1906.png/220px-Sultan_and_his_wives_at_Bangassou%2C_1906.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="162" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Sultan_and_his_wives_at_Bangassou%2C_1906.png/330px-Sultan_and_his_wives_at_Bangassou%2C_1906.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Sultan_and_his_wives_at_Bangassou%2C_1906.png/440px-Sultan_and_his_wives_at_Bangassou%2C_1906.png 2x" data-file-width="536" data-file-height="394"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Sultan_and_his_wives_at_Bangassou,_1906.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The Sultan of <a href="/wiki/Bangassou" title="Bangassou">Bangassou</a> and his wives, 1906
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>During the 16th and 17th centuries <a href="/wiki/Slave_trade" class="mw-redirect" title="Slave trade">slave traders</a> began to raid the region as part of the expansion of the Saharan and Nile River slave routes. Their captives were enslaved and shipped to the Mediterranean coast, Europe, Arabia, the Western Hemisphere, or to the slave ports and factories along the West and North Africa or South along the Ubanqui and Congo rivers.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-africanhistory.about.com_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-africanhistory.about.com-27">[27]</a></sup> In the mid 19th century, the <a href="/wiki/Bangi_language" title="Bangi language">Bobangi people</a> became major slave traders and sold their captives to the Americas using the Ubangi river to reach the coast.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> During the 18th century Bandia-Nzakara <a href="/wiki/Azande" class="mw-redirect" title="Azande">Azande</a> peoples established the <a href="/wiki/Bangassou" title="Bangassou">Bangassou</a> Kingdom along the <a href="/wiki/Ubangi_River" title="Ubangi River">Ubangi River</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-africanhistory.about.com_27-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-africanhistory.about.com-27">[27]</a></sup> In 1875, the <a href="/wiki/Sudan" title="Sudan">Sudanese</a> sultan <a href="/wiki/Rabih_az-Zubayr" title="Rabih az-Zubayr">Rabih az-Zubayr</a> governed Upper-Oubangui, which included present-day CAR.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="French_colonial_period">French colonial period</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Central_African_Republic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: French colonial period">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Ubangi-Shari" title="Ubangi-Shari">Ubangi-Shari</a>, <a href="/wiki/French_Equatorial_Africa" title="French Equatorial Africa">French Equatorial Africa</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Colonialism_in_the_Central_African_Republic" title="Colonialism in the Central African Republic">Colonialism in the Central African Republic</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The European invasion of Central African territory began in the late 19th century during the <a href="/wiki/Scramble_for_Africa" title="Scramble for Africa">Scramble for Africa</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> Europeans, primarily the French, <a href="/wiki/Germans" title="Germans">Germans</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Belgians" title="Belgians">Belgians</a>, arrived in the area in 1885. France seized and colonized <a href="/wiki/Ubangi-Shari" title="Ubangi-Shari">Ubangi-Shari</a> territory in 1894. In 1911 at the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Fez" class="mw-redirect" title="Treaty of Fez">Treaty of Fez</a>, France ceded a nearly 300,000&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> portion of the Sangha and Lobaye basins to the <a href="/wiki/German_Empire" title="German Empire">German Empire</a> which ceded a smaller area (in present-day <a href="/wiki/Chad" title="Chad">Chad</a>) to France. After <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a> France again annexed the territory. Modeled on <a href="/wiki/Leopold_II_of_Belgium" title="Leopold II of Belgium">King Leopold</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Congo_Free_State" title="Congo Free State">Congo Free State</a>, concessions were doled out to private companies that endeavored to strip the region's assets as quickly and cheaply as possible before depositing a percentage of their profits into the French treasury. The concessionary companies <a href="/wiki/Corv%C3%A9e" title="CorvÃ©e">forced local people</a> to harvest rubber, coffee, and other commodities without pay and held their families hostage until they met their quotas. Between 1890, a year after the French first arrived, and 1940, the population declined by half due to diseases, famine and exploitation by private companies.<sup id="cite_ref-fp1015_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fp1015-31">[31]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:De_Gaulle_Bangui_1940.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/De_Gaulle_Bangui_1940.jpg/220px-De_Gaulle_Bangui_1940.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="149" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/De_Gaulle_Bangui_1940.jpg/330px-De_Gaulle_Bangui_1940.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/De_Gaulle_Bangui_1940.jpg/440px-De_Gaulle_Bangui_1940.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1037" data-file-height="700"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:De_Gaulle_Bangui_1940.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Charles_de_Gaulle" title="Charles de Gaulle">Charles de Gaulle</a> in Bangui, 1940.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In 1920 <a href="/wiki/French_Equatorial_Africa" title="French Equatorial Africa">French Equatorial Africa</a> was established and Ubangi-Shari was administered from <a href="/wiki/Brazzaville" title="Brazzaville">Brazzaville</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Francophone_Africa_1997,_pg._111_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Francophone_Africa_1997,_pg._111-32">[32]</a></sup> During the 1920s and 1930s the French introduced a policy of mandatory cotton cultivation,<sup id="cite_ref-Francophone_Africa_1997,_pg._111_32-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Francophone_Africa_1997,_pg._111-32">[32]</a></sup> a network of roads was built, attempts were made to combat <a href="/wiki/African_trypanosomiasis" title="African trypanosomiasis">sleeping sickness</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Protestant" class="mw-redirect" title="Protestant">Protestant</a> <a href="/wiki/Mission_(Christianity)" class="mw-redirect" title="Mission (Christianity)">missions</a> were established to spread Christianity.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> New forms of forced labor were also introduced and a large number of Ubangians were sent to work on the <a href="/wiki/Congo-Ocean_Railway" class="mw-redirect" title="Congo-Ocean Railway">Congo-Ocean Railway</a>. Through the period of construction until 1934 there was a continual heavy cost in human lives, with total deaths among all workers along the railway estimated in excess of 17,000 of the construction workers, from a combination of both industrial accidents and diseases including <a href="/wiki/Malaria" title="Malaria">malaria</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> In 1928, a major insurrection, the <a href="/wiki/Kongo-Wara_rebellion" title="Kongo-Wara rebellion">Kongo-Wara rebellion</a> or 'war of the hoe handle', broke out in Western Ubangi-Shari and continued for several years. The extent of this insurrection, which was perhaps the largest anti-colonial rebellion in Africa during the interwar years, was carefully hidden from the French public because it provided evidence of strong opposition to French colonial rule and forced labor.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In September 1940, during the <a href="/wiki/Second_World_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Second World War">Second World War</a>, <a href="/wiki/Charles_de_Gaulle" title="Charles de Gaulle">pro-Gaullist</a> French officers took control of Ubangi-Shari and <a href="/wiki/General_Leclerc" class="mw-redirect" title="General Leclerc">General Leclerc</a> established his headquarters for the <a href="/wiki/Free_French_Forces" class="mw-redirect" title="Free French Forces">Free French Forces</a> in <a href="/wiki/Bangui" title="Bangui">Bangui</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> In 1946 <a href="/wiki/Barth%C3%A9lemy_Boganda" title="BarthÃ©lemy Boganda">BarthÃ©lemy Boganda</a> was elected with 9,000 votes to the <a href="/wiki/French_National_Assembly" class="mw-redirect" title="French National Assembly">French National Assembly</a>, becoming the first representative of the CAR in the French government. Boganda maintained a political stance against racism and the colonial regime but gradually became disheartened with the French political system and returned to CAR to establish the <a href="/wiki/Movement_for_the_Social_Evolution_of_Black_Africa" title="Movement for the Social Evolution of Black Africa">Movement for the Social Evolution of Black Africa</a> (<i>Mouvement pour l'Ã©volution sociale de l'Afrique noire</i>, MESAN) in 1950.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span id="Since_independence_.281960.E2.80.93present.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Since_independence_(1960âpresent)">Since independence (1960âpresent)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Central_African_Republic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Since independence (1960âpresent)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In the <a href="/wiki/1957_Ubangi-Shari_parliamentary_election" class="mw-redirect" title="1957 Ubangi-Shari parliamentary election">Ubangi-Shari Territorial Assembly election</a> in 1957, MESAN captured 347,000 out of the total 356,000 votes<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> and won every legislative seat,<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> which led to Boganda being elected president of the Grand Council of <a href="/wiki/French_Equatorial_Africa" title="French Equatorial Africa">French Equatorial Africa</a> and vice-president of the Ubangi-Shari Government Council.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> Within a year, he declared the establishment of the Central African Republic and served as the country's first prime minister. MESAN continued to exist, but its role was limited.<sup id="cite_ref-Kalck2005p136_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kalck2005p136-41">[41]</a></sup> After Boganda's death in a plane crash on 29 March 1959, his cousin, <a href="/wiki/David_Dacko" title="David Dacko">David Dacko</a>, took control of MESAN. Dacko became the country's first president when the CAR formally received <a href="/wiki/Independence" title="Independence">independence</a> from France on 13 August 1960, a date celebrated by the country's <a href="/wiki/List_of_national_independence_days" title="List of national independence days">Independence Day</a> holiday.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> Dacko threw out his political rivals, including <a href="/wiki/Abel_Goumba" title="Abel Goumba">Abel Goumba</a>, former Prime Minister and leader of <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Evolution_Movement_of_Central_Africa" title="Democratic Evolution Movement of Central Africa">Mouvement d'Ã©volution dÃ©mocratique de l'Afrique centrale</a> (MEDAC), whom he forced into exile in France. With all opposition parties suppressed by November 1962, Dacko declared MESAN as the official party of the state.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span id="Bokassa_and_the_Central_African_Empire_.281965.E2.80.931979.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Bokassa_and_the_Central_African_Empire_(1965â1979)">Bokassa and the Central African Empire (1965â1979)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Central_African_Republic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Bokassa and the Central African Empire (1965â1979)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Central_African_Empire" title="Central African Empire">Central African Empire</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Bokassa_colored.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Bokassa_colored.png/170px-Bokassa_colored.png" decoding="async" width="170" height="249" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Bokassa_colored.png/255px-Bokassa_colored.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Bokassa_colored.png/340px-Bokassa_colored.png 2x" data-file-width="540" data-file-height="790"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Bokassa_colored.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Jean-B%C3%A9del_Bokassa" title="Jean-BÃ©del Bokassa">Jean-BÃ©del Bokassa</a>, self-crowned <a href="/wiki/Emperor_of_Central_Africa" title="Emperor of Central Africa">Emperor of Central Africa</a><sup id="cite_ref-Bokassa_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bokassa-11">[11]</a></sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>On 31 December 1965, Dacko was overthrown in the <a href="/wiki/Saint-Sylvestre_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="Saint-Sylvestre coup d'Ã©tat">Saint-Sylvestre coup d'Ã©tat</a> by Colonel <a href="/wiki/Jean-B%C3%A9del_Bokassa" title="Jean-BÃ©del Bokassa">Jean-BÃ©del Bokassa</a>, who suspended the constitution and dissolved the National Assembly. President Bokassa declared himself President for Life in 1972 and named himself Emperor Bokassa I of the <a href="/wiki/Central_African_Empire" title="Central African Empire">Central African Empire</a> (as the country was renamed) on 4 December 1976. A year later, Emperor Bokassa crowned himself in a lavish and expensive ceremony that was ridiculed by much of the world.<sup id="cite_ref-Bokassa_11-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bokassa-11">[11]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In April 1979, young students protested against Bokassa's decree that all school attendees would need to buy uniforms from a company owned by one of his wives. The government violently suppressed the protests, killing 100 children and teenagers. Bokassa himself may have been personally involved in some of the killings.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> In September 1979, <a href="/wiki/Operation_Barracuda" title="Operation Barracuda">France overthrew Bokassa</a> and restored Dacko to power (subsequently restoring the name of the country and the original government to the Central African Republic). Dacko, in turn, was again overthrown in a <a href="/wiki/1981_Central_African_Republic_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="1981 Central African Republic coup d'Ã©tat">coup</a> by General <a href="/wiki/Andr%C3%A9_Kolingba" title="AndrÃ© Kolingba">AndrÃ© Kolingba</a> on 1 September 1981.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Central_African_Republic_under_Kolingba">Central African Republic under Kolingba</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Central_African_Republic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Central African Republic under Kolingba">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>Kolingba suspended the constitution and ruled with a military junta until 1985. He introduced a new constitution in 1986 which was adopted by a nationwide referendum. Membership in his new party, the <a href="/wiki/Rassemblement_D%C3%A9mocratique_Centrafricain" class="mw-redirect" title="Rassemblement DÃ©mocratique Centrafricain">Rassemblement DÃ©mocratique Centrafricain</a> (RDC), was voluntary. In 1987 and 1988, semi-free elections to parliament were held, but Kolingba's two major political opponents, <a href="/wiki/Abel_Goumba" title="Abel Goumba">Abel Goumba</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ange-F%C3%A9lix_Patass%C3%A9" title="Ange-FÃ©lix PatassÃ©">Ange-FÃ©lix PatassÃ©</a>, were not allowed to participate.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-46">[46]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>By 1990, inspired by the fall of the Berlin Wall, a pro-democracy movement arose. Pressure from the United States, France, and from a group of locally represented countries and agencies called GIBAFOR (France, the US, Germany, Japan, the EU, the <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a>, and the UN) finally led Kolingba to agree, in principle, to hold free elections in October 1992 with help from the UN Office of Electoral Affairs. After using the excuse of alleged irregularities to suspend the results of the elections as a pretext for holding on to power, President Kolingba came under intense pressure from GIBAFOR to establish a "Conseil National Politique Provisoire de la RÃ©publique" (Provisional National Political Council, CNPPR) and to set up a "Mixed Electoral Commission", which included representatives from all political parties.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_46-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-46">[46]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>When a second round of elections were finally held in 1993, again with the help of the international community coordinated by GIBAFOR, Ange-FÃ©lix PatassÃ© won in the second round of voting with 53% of the vote while Goumba won 45.6%. PatassÃ©'s party, the <i>Mouvement pour la LibÃ©ration du Peuple Centrafricain</i> (MLPC) or Movement for the Liberation of the Central African People, gained a simple but not an absolute majority of seats in parliament, which meant PatassÃ©'s party required coalition partners.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_46-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-46">[46]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span id="Patass.C3.A9_Government_.281993.E2.80.932003.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="PatassÃ©_Government_(1993â2003)">PatassÃ© Government (1993â2003)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Central_African_Republic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: PatassÃ© Government (1993â2003)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>PatassÃ© purged many of the Kolingba elements from the government and Kolingba supporters accused PatassÃ©'s government of conducting a "witch hunt" against the Yakoma. A new constitution was approved on 28 December 1994 but had little impact on the country's politics. In 1996â1997, reflecting steadily decreasing public confidence in the government's erratic behaviour, three mutinies against PatassÃ©'s administration were accompanied by widespread destruction of property and heightened ethnic tension. During this time (1996) the Peace Corps evacuated all its volunteers to neighboring Cameroon. To date, the Peace Corps has not returned to the Central African Republic. The <a href="/wiki/Bangui_Agreements" title="Bangui Agreements">Bangui Agreements</a>, signed in January 1997, provided for the deployment of an inter-African military mission, to Central African Republic and re-entry of ex-mutineers into the government on 7 April 1997. The inter-African military mission was later replaced by a U.N. <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council_Resolution_1159" title="United Nations Security Council Resolution 1159">peacekeeping force (MINURCA)</a>. Since 1997, the country has hosted almost a dozen peacekeeping interventions, earning it the title of "world champion of peacekeeping".<sup id="cite_ref-fp1015_31-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fp1015-31">[31]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 1998, parliamentary elections resulted in Kolingba's RDC winning 20 out of 109 seats. The next year, however, in spite of widespread public anger in urban centers over his corrupt rule, PatassÃ© won a second term in the presidential election.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On 28 May 2001, rebels stormed strategic buildings in Bangui in an <a href="/wiki/2001_Central_African_Republic_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat_attempt" title="2001 Central African Republic coup d'Ã©tat attempt">unsuccessful coup attempt</a>. The army chief of staff, Abel Abrou, and General FranÃ§ois N'Djadder Bedaya were killed, but PatassÃ© regained the upper hand by bringing in at least 300 troops of the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Democratic Republic of the Congo">Congolese</a> rebel leader <a href="/wiki/Jean-Pierre_Bemba" title="Jean-Pierre Bemba">Jean-Pierre Bemba</a> and Libyan soldiers.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In the aftermath of the <a href="/wiki/2001_Central_African_Republic_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat_attempt" title="2001 Central African Republic coup d'Ã©tat attempt">failed coup</a>, militias loyal to PatassÃ© sought revenge against rebels in many neighborhoods of <a href="/wiki/Bangui" title="Bangui">Bangui</a> and incited unrest including the murder of many political opponents. Eventually, PatassÃ© came to suspect that General <a href="/wiki/Fran%C3%A7ois_Boziz%C3%A9" title="FranÃ§ois BozizÃ©">FranÃ§ois BozizÃ©</a> was involved in another coup attempt against him, which led BozizÃ© to flee with loyal troops to Chad. In March 2003, BozizÃ© launched a surprise attack against PatassÃ©, who was out of the country. Libyan troops and some 1,000 soldiers of Bemba's Congolese rebel organization failed to stop the rebels and BozizÃ©'s forces succeeded in overthrowing PatassÃ©.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Civil_wars">Civil wars</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Central_African_Republic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Civil wars">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Rebel_in_northern_CAR_01.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Rebel_in_northern_CAR_01.jpg/220px-Rebel_in_northern_CAR_01.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Rebel_in_northern_CAR_01.jpg/330px-Rebel_in_northern_CAR_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Rebel_in_northern_CAR_01.jpg/440px-Rebel_in_northern_CAR_01.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3072" data-file-height="2048"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Rebel_in_northern_CAR_01.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Rebel militia in the northern countryside, 2007.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Central_African_Republic_Bush_War" title="Central African Republic Bush War">Central African Republic Bush War</a> and <a href="/wiki/Central_African_Republic_Civil_War" title="Central African Republic Civil War">Central African Republic Civil War</a>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Fran%C3%A7ois_Boziz%C3%A9" title="FranÃ§ois BozizÃ©">FranÃ§ois BozizÃ©</a> suspended the constitution and named a new cabinet, which included most opposition parties. <a href="/wiki/Abel_Goumba" title="Abel Goumba">Abel Goumba</a> was named vice-president, which gave BozizÃ©'s new government a positive image.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The reason for this is unclear. (September 2018)">why?</span></a></i>]</sup> BozizÃ© established a broad-based National Transition Council to draft a new constitution, and announced that he would step down and run for office once the new constitution was approved.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2004, the <a href="/wiki/Central_African_Republic_Bush_War" title="Central African Republic Bush War">Central African Republic Bush War</a> began, as forces opposed to BozizÃ© took up arms against his government. In May 2005, BozizÃ© won the presidential election, which excluded PatassÃ©, and in 2006 fighting continued between the government and the rebels.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> In November 2006, BozizÃ©'s government requested French military support to help them repel rebels who had taken control of towns in the country's northern regions.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc20061114_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc20061114-52">[52]</a></sup> Though the initially public details of the agreement pertained to logistics and intelligence, by December the French assistance included airstrikes by <a href="/wiki/Dassault_Mirage_2000" title="Dassault Mirage 2000">Dassault Mirage 2000</a> fighters against rebel positions.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bbc20061130_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc20061130-54">[54]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Syrte Agreement in February and the Birao Peace Agreement in April 2007 called for a cessation of hostilities, the billeting of <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Front_of_the_Central_African_People" title="Democratic Front of the Central African People">FDPC</a> fighters and their integration with FACA, the liberation of political prisoners, integration of FDPC into government, an amnesty for the <a href="/wiki/Union_of_Democratic_Forces_for_Unity" title="Union of Democratic Forces for Unity">UFDR</a>, its recognition as a political party, and the integration of its fighters into the national army. Several groups continued to fight but other groups signed on to the agreement, or similar agreements with the government (e.g. UFR on 15 December 2008). The only major group not to sign an agreement at the time was the <a href="/wiki/Convention_of_Patriots_for_Justice_and_Peace" title="Convention of Patriots for Justice and Peace">CPJP</a>, which continued its activities and signed a peace agreement with the government on 25 August 2012. </p>
      <p>In 2011, BozizÃ© was reelected in an election which was widely considered fraudulent.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-12">[12]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In November 2012, <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A9l%C3%A9ka" title="SÃ©lÃ©ka">SÃ©lÃ©ka</a>, a coalition of rebel groups, took over towns in the northern and central regions of the country. These groups eventually reached a peace deal with the BozizÃ©'s government in January 2013 involving a power sharing government<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_12-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-12">[12]</a></sup> but this deal broke down and the rebels seized the capital in March 2013 and BozizÃ© fled the country.<sup id="cite_ref-cnn20130324_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cnn20130324-55">[55]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-nyt20130325_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyt20130325-56">[56]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Refugees_of_the_fighting_in_the_Central_African_Republic_observe_Rwandan_soldiers_being_dropped_off_at_Bangui_M%27Poko_International_Airport_in_the_Central_African_Republic_Jan._19,_2014_140119-F-RN211-760.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Refugees_of_the_fighting_in_the_Central_African_Republic_observe_Rwandan_soldiers_being_dropped_off_at_Bangui_M%27Poko_International_Airport_in_the_Central_African_Republic_Jan._19%2C_2014_140119-F-RN211-760.jpg/220px-thumbnail.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="135" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Refugees_of_the_fighting_in_the_Central_African_Republic_observe_Rwandan_soldiers_being_dropped_off_at_Bangui_M%27Poko_International_Airport_in_the_Central_African_Republic_Jan._19%2C_2014_140119-F-RN211-760.jpg/330px-thumbnail.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Refugees_of_the_fighting_in_the_Central_African_Republic_observe_Rwandan_soldiers_being_dropped_off_at_Bangui_M%27Poko_International_Airport_in_the_Central_African_Republic_Jan._19%2C_2014_140119-F-RN211-760.jpg/440px-thumbnail.jpg 2x" data-file-width="6016" data-file-height="3693"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Refugees_of_the_fighting_in_the_Central_African_Republic_observe_Rwandan_soldiers_being_dropped_off_at_Bangui_M%27Poko_International_Airport_in_the_Central_African_Republic_Jan._19,_2014_140119-F-RN211-760.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Refugee" title="Refugee">Refugees</a> of the fighting in the Central African Republic, January 2014
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Michel_Djotodia" title="Michel Djotodia">Michel Djotodia</a> took over as president. Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Nicolas_Tiangaye" title="Nicolas Tiangaye">Nicolas Tiangaye</a> requested a <a href="/wiki/UN" class="mw-redirect" title="UN">UN</a> peacekeeping force from the <a href="/wiki/UN_Security_Council" class="mw-redirect" title="UN Security Council">UN Security Council</a> and on 31 May former President BozizÃ© was indicted for crimes against humanity and incitement of genocide.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> By the end of the year there were international warnings of a "genocide"<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> and fighting was largely from reprisal attacks on civilians from Seleka's predominantly Muslim fighters and Christian militias called "<a href="/wiki/Anti-balaka" title="Anti-balaka">anti-balaka</a>."<sup id="cite_ref-GuardianNov13_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GuardianNov13-60">[60]</a></sup> By August 2013, there were reports of over 200,000 <a href="/wiki/Internally_displaced_persons" class="mw-redirect" title="Internally displaced persons">internally displaced persons</a> (IDPs)<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:War_in_Central_African_Republic.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/War_in_Central_African_Republic.svg/250px-War_in_Central_African_Republic.svg.png" decoding="async" width="250" height="173" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/War_in_Central_African_Republic.svg/375px-War_in_Central_African_Republic.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/War_in_Central_African_Republic.svg/500px-War_in_Central_African_Republic.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1606" data-file-height="1109"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:War_in_Central_African_Republic.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Current military situation in Central African Republic
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/President_of_France" title="President of France">French President</a> <a href="/wiki/Fran%C3%A7ois_Hollande" title="FranÃ§ois Hollande">FranÃ§ois Hollande</a> called on the <a href="/wiki/UN_Security_Council" class="mw-redirect" title="UN Security Council">UN Security Council</a> and <a href="/wiki/African_Union" title="African Union">African Union</a> to increase their efforts to stabilize the country. On 18 February 2014, <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> Secretary-General <a href="/wiki/Ban_Ki-moon" title="Ban Ki-moon">Ban Ki-moon</a> called on the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council" title="United Nations Security Council">UN Security Council</a> to immediately deploy 3,000 troops to the country, bolstering the 6,000 African Union soldiers and 2,000 French troops already in the country, to combat civilians being murdered in large numbers. The <i>SÃ©lÃ©ka</i> government was said to be divided,<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> and in September 2013, Djotodia officially disbanded Seleka, but many rebels refused to disarm, becoming known as ex-Seleka, and veered further out of government control.<sup id="cite_ref-GuardianNov13_60-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GuardianNov13-60">[60]</a></sup> It is argued that the focus of the initial disarmament efforts exclusively on the Seleka inadvertently handed the anti-Balaka the upper hand, leading to the forced displacement of Muslim civilians by anti-Balaka in Bangui and western CAR.<sup id="cite_ref-fp1015_31-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fp1015-31">[31]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On 11 January 2014, Michael Djotodia and Nicolas Tiengaye resigned as part of a deal negotiated at a regional summit in neighboring <a href="/wiki/Chad" title="Chad">Chad</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Catherine_Samba-Panza" title="Catherine Samba-Panza">Catherine Samba-Panza</a> was elected as interim president by the National Transitional Council,<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> becoming the first ever female Central African president. On 23 July 2014, following Congolese mediation efforts, SÃ©lÃ©ka and anti-balaka representatives signed a ceasefire agreement in <a href="/wiki/Brazzaville" title="Brazzaville">Brazzaville</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> By the end of 2014, the country was de facto partitioned with the anti-Balaka in the southwest and ex-Seleka in the northeast.<sup id="cite_ref-fp1015_31-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fp1015-31">[31]</a></sup> In March 2015, Samantha Power, the U.S. ambassador to the United Nations, said 417 of the country's 436 mosques had been destroyed, and Muslim women were so scared of going out in public they were giving birth in their homes instead of going to the hospital.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> On 14 December 2015, SÃ©lÃ©ka rebel leaders declared an independent <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Logone" title="Republic of Logone">Republic of Logone</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span id="Touad.C3.A9ra_Government_.282016-.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="TouadÃ©ra_Government_(2016-)">TouadÃ©ra Government (2016-)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Central_African_Republic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: TouadÃ©ra Government (2016-)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/2015%E2%80%9316_Central_African_general_election" title="2015â16 Central African general election">Presidential Elections</a> were held in December 2015. As no candidate received more than 50% of the vote, a second round of elections was held on 14 February 2016 with run-offs on 31 March 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> In the second round of voting, former Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Faustin-Archange_Touad%C3%A9ra" title="Faustin-Archange TouadÃ©ra">Faustin-Archange TouadÃ©ra</a> was declared the winner with 63% of the vote, defeating <a href="/wiki/Union_for_Central_African_Renewal" title="Union for Central African Renewal">Union for Central African Renewal</a> candidate <a href="/wiki/Anicet-Georges_Dologu%C3%A9l%C3%A9" title="Anicet-Georges DologuÃ©lÃ©">Anicet-Georges DologuÃ©lÃ©</a>, another former Prime Minister.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> While the elections suffered from many potential voters being absent as they had taken refuge in other countries, the fears of widespread violence were ultimately unfounded and the <a href="/wiki/African_Union" title="African Union">African Union</a> regarded the elections as successful.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>TouadÃ©ra was sworn in on 30 March 2016. No representatives of the Seleka rebel group or the "anti-balaka" militias were included in the subsequently formed government.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>After the end of TouadÃ©ra's first term, <a href="/wiki/2020%E2%80%9321_Central_African_general_election" title="2020â21 Central African general election">Presidential Elections</a> were held on 27 December 2020 with a possible second round planned for 14 February 2021.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> Former president <a href="/wiki/Fran%C3%A7ois_Boziz%C3%A9" title="FranÃ§ois BozizÃ©">FranÃ§ois BozizÃ©</a> announced his candidacy on 25 July 2020 but was rejected by the Constitutional Court of the country, which held that BozizÃ© did not satisfy the âgood moralityâ requirement for candidates because of an international warrant and <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> sanctions against him for alleged assassinations, torture and other crimes.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>As large parts of the country were at the time controlled by armed groups, the election could not be conducted in many areas of the country.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> Some 800 of the country's polling stations, 14% of the total, were closed due to violence.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> Three <a href="/wiki/Burundi" title="Burundi">Burundian</a> peacekeepers were killed and an additional two were wounded during the run-up to the election.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-UNNews_261220_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNNews_261220-80">[80]</a></sup> President Faustin Archange TouadÃ©ra was reelected in the first round of the election in December 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Central_African_Republic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_the_Central_African_Republic" title="Geography of the Central African Republic">Geography of the Central African Republic</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Republique_Centrafricaine_-_Boali_-_Chutes_de_Boali.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Republique_Centrafricaine_-_Boali_-_Chutes_de_Boali.jpg/170px-Republique_Centrafricaine_-_Boali_-_Chutes_de_Boali.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="256" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Republique_Centrafricaine_-_Boali_-_Chutes_de_Boali.jpg/255px-Republique_Centrafricaine_-_Boali_-_Chutes_de_Boali.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Republique_Centrafricaine_-_Boali_-_Chutes_de_Boali.jpg/340px-Republique_Centrafricaine_-_Boali_-_Chutes_de_Boali.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2368" data-file-height="3567"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Republique_Centrafricaine_-_Boali_-_Chutes_de_Boali.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Falls of Boali on the Mbali River
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:CARvillagefromthesky.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/CARvillagefromthesky.jpg/220px-CARvillagefromthesky.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/CARvillagefromthesky.jpg/330px-CARvillagefromthesky.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/CARvillagefromthesky.jpg/440px-CARvillagefromthesky.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="683"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:CARvillagefromthesky.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A village in the Central African Republic
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The Central African Republic is a landlocked nation within the interior of the African continent. It is bordered by Cameroon, Chad, Sudan, South Sudan, the Democratic Republic of the Congo, and the Republic of the Congo. The country lies between latitudes <a href="/wiki/2nd_parallel_north" title="2nd parallel north">2Â°</a> and <a href="/wiki/11th_parallel_north" title="11th parallel north">11Â°N</a>, and longitudes <a href="/wiki/14th_meridian_east" title="14th meridian east">14Â°</a> and <a href="/wiki/28th_meridian_east" title="28th meridian east">28Â°E</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-82">[82]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Much of the country consists of flat or rolling plateau <a href="/wiki/Savanna" title="Savanna">savanna</a> approximately 500 metres (1,640&nbsp;ft) above <a href="/wiki/Sea_level" title="Sea level">sea level</a>. In addition to the Fertit Hills in the northeast of the CAR, there are scattered hills in the southwest regions. In the northwest is the Yade Massif, a <a href="/wiki/Granite" title="Granite">granite</a> plateau with an altitude of 348 metres (1,143&nbsp;ft). The CAR contains six terrestrial ecoregions: <a href="/wiki/Northeastern_Congolian_lowland_forests" title="Northeastern Congolian lowland forests">Northeastern Congolian lowland forests</a>, <a href="/wiki/Northwestern_Congolian_lowland_forests" title="Northwestern Congolian lowland forests">Northwestern Congolian lowland forests</a>, <a href="/wiki/Western_Congolian_swamp_forests" title="Western Congolian swamp forests">Western Congolian swamp forests</a>, <a href="/wiki/East_Sudanian_savanna" title="East Sudanian savanna">East Sudanian savanna</a>, <a href="/wiki/Northern_Congolian_forest-savanna_mosaic" class="mw-redirect" title="Northern Congolian forest-savanna mosaic">Northern Congolian forest-savanna mosaic</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sahelian_Acacia_savanna" class="mw-redirect" title="Sahelian Acacia savanna">Sahelian Acacia savanna</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-DinersteinOlson2017_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DinersteinOlson2017-83">[83]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>At 622,984 square kilometres (240,535&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi), the Central African Republic is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_and_dependencies_by_area" title="List of countries and dependencies by area">world's 44th-largest country</a>. It is comparable in size to <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukraine</a>, as the <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukraine</a> is 603,500 square kilometres (233,000&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi) in area, according to <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_and_dependencies_by_area" title="List of countries and dependencies by area">List of countries and dependencies by area</a>. </p>
      <p>Much of the southern border is formed by <a href="/wiki/Tributary" title="Tributary">tributaries</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Congo_River" title="Congo River">Congo River</a>; the <a href="/wiki/Mbomou_River" title="Mbomou River">Mbomou River</a> in the east merges with the <a href="/wiki/Uele_River" title="Uele River">Uele River</a> to form the <a href="/wiki/Ubangi_River" title="Ubangi River">Ubangi River</a>, which also comprises portions of the southern border. The <a href="/wiki/Sangha_River" title="Sangha River">Sangha River</a> flows through some of the western regions of the country, while the eastern border lies along the edge of the <a href="/wiki/Nile_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Nile River">Nile River</a> <a href="/wiki/Drainage_basin" title="Drainage basin">watershed</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_82-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-82">[82]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>It has been estimated that up to 8% of the country is covered by forest, with the densest parts generally located in the southern regions. The forests are highly diverse and include commercially important species of <a href="/wiki/Ayous" class="mw-redirect" title="Ayous">Ayous</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sapele" title="Sapele">Sapelli</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sipo_(timber)" class="mw-redirect" title="Sipo (timber)">Sipo</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> The deforestation rate is about 0.4% per annum, and <a href="/wiki/Illegal_logging" title="Illegal logging">lumber poaching</a> is commonplace.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> The Central African Republic had a 2018 <a href="/wiki/Forest_Landscape_Integrity_Index" title="Forest Landscape Integrity Index">Forest Landscape Integrity Index</a> mean score of 9.28/10, ranking it 7th globally out of 172 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-FLII-Supplementary_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FLII-Supplementary-86">[86]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2008, Central African Republic was the world's least <a href="/wiki/Light_pollution" title="Light pollution">light pollution</a> affected country.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Central African Republic is the focal point of the <a href="/wiki/Bangui_Magnetic_Anomaly" class="mw-redirect" title="Bangui Magnetic Anomaly">Bangui Magnetic Anomaly</a>, one of the largest magnetic anomalies on Earth.<sup id="cite_ref-LPI_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LPI-88">[88]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Wildlife">Wildlife</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Central_African_Republic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Wildlife">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Wildlife_of_the_Central_African_Republic" title="Wildlife of the Central African Republic">Wildlife of the Central African Republic</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Dzanga.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Dzanga.jpg/220px-Dzanga.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="141" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Dzanga.jpg/330px-Dzanga.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Dzanga.jpg/440px-Dzanga.jpg 2x" data-file-width="750" data-file-height="480"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Dzanga.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Dzanga-Sangha_Reserve" class="mw-redirect" title="Dzanga-Sangha Reserve">Dzanga-Sangha Reserve</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In the southwest, the Dzanga-Sangha National Park is located in a rain forest area. The country is noted for its population of <a href="/wiki/Forest_elephant" class="mw-redirect" title="Forest elephant">forest elephants</a> and <a href="/wiki/Western_lowland_gorilla" title="Western lowland gorilla">western lowland gorillas</a>. In the north, the <a href="/wiki/Manovo-Gounda_St_Floris_National_Park" class="mw-redirect" title="Manovo-Gounda St Floris National Park">Manovo-Gounda St Floris National Park</a> is well-populated with wildlife, including <a href="/wiki/African_leopard" title="African leopard">leopards</a>, <a href="/wiki/Central_African_lion" class="mw-redirect" title="Central African lion">lions</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sudan_cheetah" class="mw-redirect" title="Sudan cheetah">cheetahs</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rhinoceros" title="Rhinoceros">rhinos</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Bamingui-Bangoran_National_Park" class="mw-redirect" title="Bamingui-Bangoran National Park">Bamingui-Bangoran National Park</a> is located in the northeast of CAR. The parks have been seriously affected by the activities of poachers, particularly those from <a href="/wiki/Sudan" title="Sudan">Sudan</a>, over the past two decades.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Central_African_Republic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Climate_of_the_Central_African_Republic" class="mw-redirect" title="Climate of the Central African Republic">Climate of the Central African Republic</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Koppen-Geiger_Map_CAF_present.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Koppen-Geiger_Map_CAF_present.svg/260px-Koppen-Geiger_Map_CAF_present.svg.png" decoding="async" width="260" height="156" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Koppen-Geiger_Map_CAF_present.svg/390px-Koppen-Geiger_Map_CAF_present.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Koppen-Geiger_Map_CAF_present.svg/520px-Koppen-Geiger_Map_CAF_present.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1414" data-file-height="850"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Koppen-Geiger_Map_CAF_present.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Central African Republic map of KÃ¶ppen climate classification.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The climate of the Central African Republic is generally <a href="/wiki/Tropics" title="Tropics">tropical</a>, with a <a href="/wiki/Wet_season" title="Wet season">wet season</a> that lasts from June to September in the northern regions of the country, and from May to October in the south. During the wet season, rainstorms are an almost daily occurrence, and early morning <a href="/wiki/Fog" title="Fog">fog</a> is commonplace. Maximum annual precipitation is approximately 1,800 millimetres (71&nbsp;in) in the upper Ubangi region.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The northern areas are hot and humid from February to May,<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> but can be subject to the hot, dry, and dusty <a href="/wiki/Trade_wind" class="mw-redirect" title="Trade wind">trade wind</a> known as the <a href="/wiki/Harmattan" title="Harmattan">Harmattan</a>. The southern regions have a more equatorial climate, but they are subject to <a href="/wiki/Desertification" title="Desertification">desertification</a>, while the extreme northeast regions of the country are a <a href="/wiki/Steppe" title="Steppe">steppe</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Prefectures_and_sub-prefectures">Prefectures and sub-prefectures</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Central_African_Republic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Prefectures and sub-prefectures">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Prefectures_of_the_Central_African_Republic" title="Prefectures of the Central African Republic">Prefectures of the Central African Republic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sub-prefectures_of_the_Central_African_Republic" title="Sub-prefectures of the Central African Republic">Sub-prefectures of the Central African Republic</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:452px;">
        <div class="noresize">
         <map name="ImageMap_4e08c21cf17b4815"><area href="/wiki/Bangui" shape="rect" coords="149,224,192,241" alt="Bangui" title="Bangui"><area href="/wiki/Sangha-Mba%C3%A9r%C3%A9" shape="rect" coords="11,269,64,303" alt="Sangha-MbaÃ©rÃ©" title="Sangha-MbaÃ©rÃ©"><area href="/wiki/Mamb%C3%A9r%C3%A9-Kad%C3%A9%C3%AF" shape="rect" coords="25,207,85,247" alt="MambÃ©rÃ©-KadÃ©Ã¯" title="MambÃ©rÃ©-KadÃ©Ã¯"><area href="/wiki/Nana-Mamb%C3%A9r%C3%A9" shape="rect" coords="14,163,75,202" alt="Nana-MambÃ©rÃ©" title="Nana-MambÃ©rÃ©"><area href="/wiki/Ouham-Pend%C3%A9" shape="rect" coords="34,123,85,157" alt="Ouham-PendÃ©" title="Ouham-PendÃ©"><area href="/wiki/Ouham" shape="rect" coords="95,134,138,163" alt="Ouham" title="Ouham"><area href="/wiki/Ombella-M%27Poko" shape="rect" coords="96,191,149,213" alt="Ombella-M'Poko" title="Ombella-M'Poko"><area href="/wiki/Lobaye" shape="rect" coords="96,224,132,247" alt="Lobaye" title="Lobaye"><area href="/wiki/Nana-Gr%C3%A9bizi" shape="rect" coords="149,123,185,151" alt="Nana-GrÃ©bizi" title="Nana-GrÃ©bizi"><area href="/wiki/K%C3%A9mo" shape="rect" coords="149,168,170,191" alt="KÃ©mo" title="KÃ©mo"><area href="/wiki/Ouaka" shape="rect" coords="192,157,227,179" alt="Ouaka" title="Ouaka"><area href="/wiki/Basse-Kotto" shape="rect" coords="196,213,256,238" alt="Basse-Kotto" title="Basse-Kotto"><area href="/wiki/Bamingui-Bangoran" shape="rect" coords="165,67,227,112" alt="Bamingui-Bangoran" title="Bamingui-Bangoran"><area href="/wiki/Vakaga" shape="rect" coords="245,34,298,62" alt="Vakaga" title="Vakaga"><area href="/wiki/Haute-Kotto" shape="rect" coords="245,106,319,146" alt="Haute-Kotto" title="Haute-Kotto"><area href="/wiki/Mbomou" shape="rect" coords="252,168,319,207" alt="Mbomou" title="Mbomou"><area href="/wiki/Haut-Mbomou" shape="rect" coords="351,151,409,202" alt="Haut-Mbomou" title="Haut-Mbomou"></map>
         <img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/CAR_map_of_prefectures.svg/450px-CAR_map_of_prefectures.svg.png" decoding="async" width="450" height="311" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/CAR_map_of_prefectures.svg/675px-CAR_map_of_prefectures.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/CAR_map_of_prefectures.svg/900px-CAR_map_of_prefectures.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1606" data-file-height="1110" usemap="#ImageMap_4e08c21cf17b4815">
        </div> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:CAR_map_of_prefectures.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A clickable map of the fourteen prefectures of the Central African Republic.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The Central African Republic is divided into 16 administrative <a href="/wiki/Prefecture" title="Prefecture">prefectures</a> (<i>prÃ©fectures</i>), two of which are economic prefectures (<i>prÃ©fectures economiques</i>), and one an autonomous <a href="/wiki/Commune_(subnational_entity)" class="mw-redirect" title="Commune (subnational entity)">commune</a>; the prefectures are further divided into 71 sub-prefectures (<i>sous-prÃ©fectures</i>).<sup id="cite_ref-:3_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-93">[93]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Prefectures_of_the_Central_African_Republic" title="Prefectures of the Central African Republic">prefectures</a> are <a href="/wiki/Bamingui-Bangoran" title="Bamingui-Bangoran">Bamingui-Bangoran</a>, <a href="/wiki/Basse-Kotto" title="Basse-Kotto">Basse-Kotto</a>, <a href="/wiki/Haute-Kotto" title="Haute-Kotto">Haute-Kotto</a>, <a href="/wiki/Haut-Mbomou" title="Haut-Mbomou">Haut-Mbomou</a>, <a href="/wiki/K%C3%A9mo" title="KÃ©mo">KÃ©mo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lobaye" title="Lobaye">Lobaye</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mamb%C3%A9r%C3%A9-Kad%C3%A9%C3%AF" title="MambÃ©rÃ©-KadÃ©Ã¯">MambÃ©rÃ©-KadÃ©Ã¯</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mbomou" title="Mbomou">Mbomou</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nana-Mamb%C3%A9r%C3%A9" title="Nana-MambÃ©rÃ©">Nana-MambÃ©rÃ©</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ombella-M%27Poko" title="Ombella-M'Poko">Ombella-M'Poko</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ouaka" title="Ouaka">Ouaka</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ouham" title="Ouham">Ouham</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ouham-Pend%C3%A9" title="Ouham-PendÃ©">Ouham-PendÃ©</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vakaga" title="Vakaga">Vakaga</a>. The economic prefectures are <a href="/wiki/Nana-Gr%C3%A9bizi" title="Nana-GrÃ©bizi">Nana-GrÃ©bizi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sangha-Mba%C3%A9r%C3%A9" title="Sangha-MbaÃ©rÃ©">Sangha-MbaÃ©rÃ©</a>, while the commune is the capital city of <a href="/wiki/Bangui" title="Bangui">Bangui</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:3_93-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-93">[93]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Central_African_Republic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Group_of_Peul_women_in_Paoua.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Group_of_Peul_women_in_Paoua.jpg/220px-Group_of_Peul_women_in_Paoua.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Group_of_Peul_women_in_Paoua.jpg/330px-Group_of_Peul_women_in_Paoua.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Group_of_Peul_women_in_Paoua.jpg/440px-Group_of_Peul_women_in_Paoua.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="683"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Group_of_Peul_women_in_Paoua.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Fula women in <a href="/wiki/Paoua" title="Paoua">Paoua</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_the_Central_African_Republic" title="Demographics of the Central African Republic">Demographics of the Central African Republic</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The population of the Central African Republic has almost quadrupled since independence. In 1960, the population was 1,232,000; as of a 2018 UN estimate, it is approximately 4,666,368.<sup id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP-2">[2]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_2019_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP_2019-3">[3]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> estimates that approximately 4% of the population aged between 15 and 49 is <a href="/wiki/HIV" title="HIV">HIV</a> positive.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> Only 3% of the country has <a href="/wiki/Antiretroviral" class="mw-redirect" title="Antiretroviral">antiretroviral</a> therapy available, compared to a 17% coverage in the neighbouring countries of <a href="/wiki/Chad" title="Chad">Chad</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Republic of the Congo">Republic of the Congo</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The nation is divided into over 80 ethnic groups, each having its own language. The largest ethnic groups are the <a href="/wiki/Baggara" class="mw-redirect" title="Baggara">Baggara Arabs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Baka_people_(Cameroon_and_Gabon)" title="Baka people (Cameroon and Gabon)">Baka</a>, <a href="/wiki/Banda_people" title="Banda people">Banda</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aka_people" title="Aka people">Bayaka</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fula_people" title="Fula people">Fula</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gbaya_people" title="Gbaya people">Gbaya</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kara_people" title="Kara people">Kara</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kresh_people" title="Kresh people">Kresh</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mbaka_people" title="Mbaka people">Mbaka</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mandja_people" title="Mandja people">Mandja</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ngbandi_people" title="Ngbandi people">Ngbandi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sara_people" title="Sara people">Sara</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vidiri_people" title="Vidiri people">Vidiri</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wodaabe" title="Wodaabe">Wodaabe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yakoma_people" title="Yakoma people">Yakoma</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yulu_people" title="Yulu people">Yulu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zande_people" title="Zande people">Zande</a>, with <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_the_Central_African_Republic#Ethnic_groups" title="Demographics of the Central African Republic">others</a> including <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_groups_in_Europe" title="Ethnic groups in Europe">Europeans</a> of mostly <a href="/wiki/French_people" title="French people">French descent</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_12-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-12">[12]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><br> </p>
