      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Central_African_Republic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_the_Central_African_Republic" title="Religion in the Central African Republic">Religion in the Central African Republic</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Niem_(RCA)_-_Eglise_de_brousse_1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Niem_%28RCA%29_-_Eglise_de_brousse_1.jpg/220px-Niem_%28RCA%29_-_Eglise_de_brousse_1.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Niem_%28RCA%29_-_Eglise_de_brousse_1.jpg/330px-Niem_%28RCA%29_-_Eglise_de_brousse_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Niem_%28RCA%29_-_Eglise_de_brousse_1.jpg/440px-Niem_%28RCA%29_-_Eglise_de_brousse_1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3008" data-file-height="2000"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Niem_(RCA)_-_Eglise_de_brousse_1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A Christian church in the Central African Republic.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>According to the 2003 national census, 80.3% of the population was <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christian</a> (51.4% <a href="/wiki/Protestantism" title="Protestantism">Protestant</a> and 28.9% <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholicism">Roman Catholic</a>), 10% was <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Muslim</a> and 4.5 percent other religious groups, with 5.5 percent having no religious beliefs.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> More recent work from the Pew Research Center estimated that, as of 2010, Christians constituted 89.8% of the population (60.7% Protestant and 28.5% Catholic) while Muslims made up 8.9%.<sup id="cite_ref-Pew_Christians_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pew_Christians-99">[99]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Pew_Muslims_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pew_Muslims-100">[100]</a></sup> The Catholic Church claims over 1.5&nbsp;million adherents, approximately one-third of the population.<sup id="cite_ref-Catholic_Stats_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Catholic_Stats-101">[101]</a></sup> Indigenous belief (<a href="/wiki/Animism" title="Animism">animism</a>) is also practiced, and many indigenous beliefs are <a href="/wiki/Religious_syncretism" title="Religious syncretism">incorporated into</a> Christian and Islamic practice.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> A UN director described religious tensions between Muslims and Christians as being high.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>There are many missionary groups operating in the country, including <a href="/wiki/Lutheranism" title="Lutheranism">Lutherans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Baptists" title="Baptists">Baptists</a>, <a href="/wiki/Catholicism" class="mw-redirect" title="Catholicism">Catholics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fellowship_of_Grace_Brethren_Churches" class="mw-redirect" title="Fellowship of Grace Brethren Churches">Grace Brethren</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Jehovah%27s_Witnesses" title="Jehovah's Witnesses">Jehovah's Witnesses</a>. While these missionaries are predominantly from the United States, France, Italy, and Spain, many are also from <a href="/wiki/Nigeria" title="Nigeria">Nigeria</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Democratic Republic of the Congo">Democratic Republic of the Congo</a>, and other African countries. Large numbers of missionaries left the country when fighting broke out between rebel and government forces in 2002â3, but many of them have now returned to continue their work.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>According to Overseas Development Institute research, during the crisis ongoing since 2012, religious leaders have mediated between communities and armed groups; they also provided refuge for people seeking shelter.<sup id="cite_ref-odi.org_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-odi.org-105">[105]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Central_African_Republic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_the_Central_African_Republic" title="Languages of the Central African Republic">Languages of the Central African Republic</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The Central African Republic's two official languages are <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sango_language" title="Sango language">Sango</a> (also spelled Sangho),<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> a <a href="/wiki/Creole_language" title="Creole language">creole</a> developed as an inter-ethnic <a href="/wiki/Lingua_franca" title="Lingua franca">lingua franca</a> based on the local <a href="/wiki/Ngbandi_language" title="Ngbandi language">Ngbandi language</a>. CAR is one of the few African countries to have an <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Africa" title="Languages of Africa">African language</a> as their official language. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Central_African_Republic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_African_writers_by_country#Central_African_Republic" title="List of African writers by country">List of African writers by country Â§&nbsp;Central African Republic</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Music_of_the_Central_African_Republic" title="Music of the Central African Republic">Music of the Central African Republic</a>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Central_African_Republic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Mass_media_in_the_Central_African_Republic" title="Mass media in the Central African Republic">Mass media in the Central African Republic</a>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Central_African_Republic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Central_African_Republic_at_the_Olympics" title="Central African Republic at the Olympics">Central African Republic at the Olympics</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Basketball is the country's most popular sport and a good way to connect with its people.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup> Its <a href="/wiki/Central_African_Republic_national_basketball_team" class="mw-redirect" title="Central African Republic national basketball team">national team</a> won the <a href="/wiki/AfroBasket" title="AfroBasket">African Championship</a> twice and was the first Sub-Saharan African team to qualify for the <a href="/wiki/Basketball_World_Cup" class="mw-redirect" title="Basketball World Cup">Basketball World Cup</a>, in <a href="/wiki/1974_FIBA_World_Championship" title="1974 FIBA World Championship">1974</a>. </p>
      <p>The country also has a <a href="/wiki/Central_African_Republic_national_football_team" title="Central African Republic national football team">national football team</a>, which is governed by the <a href="/wiki/Central_African_Football_Federation" title="Central African Football Federation">Central African Football Federation</a>, and stages matches at the <a href="/wiki/Barth%C3%A9lemy_Boganda_Stadium" title="BarthÃ©lemy Boganda Stadium">BarthÃ©lemy Boganda Stadium</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics_and_government">Politics and government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Central_African_Republic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Politics and government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_the_Central_African_Republic" title="Politics of the Central African Republic">Politics of the Central African Republic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Central_African_Republic_Council_of_Ministers" title="Central African Republic Council of Ministers">Central African Republic Council of Ministers</a>, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_political_parties_in_the_Central_African_Republic" title="List of political parties in the Central African Republic">List of political parties in the Central African Republic</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Secretary_Pompeo_meets_with_Central_African_Republic_President_Faustin-Archange_Touadera_(33709600898).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Secretary_Pompeo_meets_with_Central_African_Republic_President_Faustin-Archange_Touadera_%2833709600898%29.jpg/220px-Secretary_Pompeo_meets_with_Central_African_Republic_President_Faustin-Archange_Touadera_%2833709600898%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Secretary_Pompeo_meets_with_Central_African_Republic_President_Faustin-Archange_Touadera_%2833709600898%29.jpg/330px-Secretary_Pompeo_meets_with_Central_African_Republic_President_Faustin-Archange_Touadera_%2833709600898%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Secretary_Pompeo_meets_with_Central_African_Republic_President_Faustin-Archange_Touadera_%2833709600898%29.jpg/440px-Secretary_Pompeo_meets_with_Central_African_Republic_President_Faustin-Archange_Touadera_%2833709600898%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2000" data-file-height="1333"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Secretary_Pompeo_meets_with_Central_African_Republic_President_Faustin-Archange_Touadera_(33709600898).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Central African Republic President <a href="/wiki/Faustin_Touadera" class="mw-redirect" title="Faustin Touadera">Faustin Touadera</a> with U.S. Secretary of State <a href="/wiki/Mike_Pompeo" title="Mike Pompeo">Mike Pompeo</a>, 11 April 2019
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Politics in the Central African Republic formally take place in a framework of a <a href="/wiki/Semi-presidential_system" title="Semi-presidential system">semi-presidential</a> <a href="/wiki/Republic" title="Republic">republic</a>. In this system, the <a href="/wiki/Heads_of_state_of_the_Central_African_Republic_(and_Central_African_Empire)" class="mw-redirect" title="Heads of state of the Central African Republic (and Central African Empire)">President</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">head of state</a>, with a <a href="/wiki/Heads_of_government_of_the_Central_African_Republic_(and_Central_African_Empire)" class="mw-redirect" title="Heads of government of the Central African Republic (and Central African Empire)">Prime Minister</a> as <a href="/wiki/Head_of_government" title="Head of government">head of government</a>. <a href="/wiki/Executive_power" class="mw-redirect" title="Executive power">Executive power</a> is exercised by the government. <a href="/wiki/Legislative_power" class="mw-redirect" title="Legislative power">Legislative power</a> is vested in both the government and parliament.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_12-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-12">[12]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Changes in government have occurred in recent years by three methods: violence, negotiations, and elections. A new constitution was approved by voters in a referendum held on 5 December 2004. The government was rated 'Partly Free' from 1991 to 2001 and from 2004 to 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Executive_branch">Executive branch</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Central_African_Republic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Executive branch">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The president is elected by popular vote for a six-year term, and the prime minister is appointed by the president. The president also appoints and presides over the <a href="/wiki/Central_African_Republic_Council_of_Ministers" title="Central African Republic Council of Ministers">Council of Ministers</a>, which initiates laws and oversees government operations. However, as of 2018 the official government is not in control of large parts of the country, which are governed by rebel groups.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Acting president since April 2016 is <a href="/wiki/Faustin_Archange_Touadera" class="mw-redirect" title="Faustin Archange Touadera">Faustin Archange Touadera</a> who followed the interim government under <a href="/wiki/Catherine_Samba-Panza" title="Catherine Samba-Panza">Catherine Samba-Panza</a>, interim prime minister <a href="/wiki/Andr%C3%A9_Nzapayek%C3%A9" title="AndrÃ© NzapayekÃ©">AndrÃ© NzapayekÃ©</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Legislative_branch">Legislative branch</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Central_African_Republic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Legislative branch">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/National_Assembly_of_the_Central_African_Republic" class="mw-redirect" title="National Assembly of the Central African Republic">National Assembly</a> (<i>AssemblÃ©e Nationale</i>) has 140 members, elected for a five-year term using the two-round (or <a href="/wiki/Two-round_system" title="Two-round system">Run-off</a>) system.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_12-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-12">[12]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Judicial_branch">Judicial branch</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Central_African_Republic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Judicial branch">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>As in many other former French colonies, the Central African Republic's legal system is based on <a href="/wiki/French_law" class="mw-redirect" title="French law">French law</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup> The Supreme Court, or <i>Cour Supreme</i>, is made up of judges appointed by the president. There is also a Constitutional Court, and its judges are also appointed by the president.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_12-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-12">[12]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Central_African_Republic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Foreign relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Central_African_Armed_Forces" title="Central African Armed Forces">Central African Armed Forces</a> and <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_the_Central_African_Republic" title="Foreign relations of the Central African Republic">Foreign relations of the Central African Republic</a>
      </div>
      <p>The Central African Republic relies heavily on Russian mercenaries for the protection of its diamond mines.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup></p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Vladimir_Putin_and_Faustin_Touadera,_23_may_2018_(1).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Vladimir_Putin_and_Faustin_Touadera%2C_23_may_2018_%281%29.jpg/220px-Vladimir_Putin_and_Faustin_Touadera%2C_23_may_2018_%281%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="136" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Vladimir_Putin_and_Faustin_Touadera%2C_23_may_2018_%281%29.jpg/330px-Vladimir_Putin_and_Faustin_Touadera%2C_23_may_2018_%281%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Vladimir_Putin_and_Faustin_Touadera%2C_23_may_2018_%281%29.jpg/440px-Vladimir_Putin_and_Faustin_Touadera%2C_23_may_2018_%281%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1880" data-file-height="1160"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Vladimir_Putin_and_Faustin_Touadera,_23_may_2018_(1).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>President <a href="/wiki/Faustin_Touadera" class="mw-redirect" title="Faustin Touadera">Faustin Touadera</a> with Russian President <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Putin" title="Vladimir Putin">Vladimir Putin</a>, 23 May 2018
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_aid_and_UN_Involvement">Foreign aid and UN Involvement</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Central_African_Republic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Foreign aid and UN Involvement">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>The Central African Republic is heavily dependent upon foreign <a href="/wiki/Aid" title="Aid">aid</a> and numerous <a href="/wiki/Non-governmental_organization" title="Non-governmental organization">NGOs</a> provide services that the government does not provide.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup> In 2019, over US$100&nbsp;million in foreign aid was spent in the country, mostly on humanitarian assistance.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2006, due to ongoing violence, over 50,000 people in the country's northwest were at risk of starvation<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup> but this was averted due to assistance from the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-UNreport_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNreport-118">[118]</a></sup> On 8 January 2008, the UN Secretary-General Ban Ki-Moon declared that the Central African Republic was eligible to receive assistance from the Peacebuilding Fund.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup> Three priority areas were identified: first, the reform of the security sector; second, the promotion of good governance and the rule of law; and third, the revitalization of communities affected by conflicts. On 12 June 2008, the Central African Republic requested assistance from the <a href="/wiki/UN_Peacebuilding_Commission" class="mw-redirect" title="UN Peacebuilding Commission">UN Peacebuilding Commission</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup> which was set up in 2005 to help countries emerging from conflict avoid devolving back into war or chaos.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In response to concerns of a potential genocide, a peacekeeping force â the International Support Mission to the Central African Republic (MISCA) â was authorized in December 2013. This African Union force of 6,000 personnel was accompanied by the French Operation Sangaris.<sup id="cite_ref-odi.org_105-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-odi.org-105">[105]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2017, Central African Republic signed the UN <a href="/wiki/Treaty_on_the_Prohibition_of_Nuclear_Weapons" title="Treaty on the Prohibition of Nuclear Weapons">treaty on the Prohibition of Nuclear Weapons</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Human_rights">Human rights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Central_African_Republic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Human rights">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_the_Central_African_Republic" title="Human rights in the Central African Republic">Human rights in the Central African Republic</a>, <a href="/wiki/LGBT_rights_in_the_Central_African_Republic" title="LGBT rights in the Central African Republic">LGBT rights in the Central African Republic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Child_marriage_in_the_Central_African_Republic" title="Child marriage in the Central African Republic">Child marriage in the Central African Republic</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Polygamy_in_the_Central_African_Republic" title="Polygamy in the Central African Republic">Polygamy in the Central African Republic</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The 2009 Human Rights Report by the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_State" title="United States Department of State">United States Department of State</a> noted that human rights in CAR were poor and expressed concerns over numerous government abuses.<sup id="cite_ref-2009_Human_Rights_Report_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2009_Human_Rights_Report-123">[123]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/United_States_State_Department" class="mw-redirect" title="United States State Department">U.S. State Department</a> alleged that major human rights abuses such as <a href="/wiki/Extrajudicial_punishment" title="Extrajudicial punishment">extrajudicial executions</a> by security forces, <a href="/wiki/Torture" title="Torture">torture</a>, beatings and <a href="/wiki/Rape" title="Rape">rape</a> of suspects and prisoners occurred with impunity. It also alleged harsh and life-threatening conditions in <a href="/wiki/Prison" title="Prison">prisons</a> and detention centers, <a href="/wiki/Arbitrary_arrest_and_detention" title="Arbitrary arrest and detention">arbitrary arrest</a>, prolonged <a href="/wiki/Remand_(detention)" title="Remand (detention)">pretrial detention</a> and denial of a <a href="/wiki/Right_to_a_fair_trial" title="Right to a fair trial">fair trial</a>, restrictions on freedom of movement, official <a href="/wiki/Corruption" title="Corruption">corruption</a>, and restrictions on <a href="/wiki/Labor_rights" title="Labor rights">workers' rights</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-2009_Human_Rights_Report_123-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2009_Human_Rights_Report-123">[123]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Living_on_the_rainforest.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Living_on_the_rainforest.jpg/220px-Living_on_the_rainforest.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Living_on_the_rainforest.jpg/330px-Living_on_the_rainforest.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Living_on_the_rainforest.jpg/440px-Living_on_the_rainforest.jpg 2x" data-file-width="958" data-file-height="636"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Living_on_the_rainforest.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/Aka_people" title="Aka people">Aka Pygmies</a> living in the <a href="/wiki/Dzanga-Sangha_Special_Reserve" title="Dzanga-Sangha Special Reserve">Dzanga-Sangha Special Reserve</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The State Department report also cites widespread <a href="/wiki/Riot" title="Riot">mob violence</a>, the prevalence of <a href="/wiki/Female_genital_mutilation" title="Female genital mutilation">female genital mutilation</a>, discrimination against women and <a href="/wiki/Pygmy_peoples" title="Pygmy peoples">Pygmies</a>, <a href="/wiki/Human_trafficking" title="Human trafficking">human trafficking</a>, <a href="/wiki/Unfree_labour" class="mw-redirect" title="Unfree labour">forced labor</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Child_labor" class="mw-redirect" title="Child labor">child labor</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup> Freedom of movement is limited in the northern part of the country "because of actions by state security forces, armed bandits, and other nonstate armed entities", and due to fighting between government and anti-government forces, many persons have been <a href="/wiki/Internally_displaced_person" title="Internally displaced person">internally displaced</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-state.gov_125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-state.gov-125">[125]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Violence against children and women in relation to accusations of <a href="/wiki/Witchcraft" title="Witchcraft">witchcraft</a> has also been cited as a serious problem in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-unicef.org_126-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unicef.org-126">[126]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup> Witchcraft is a criminal offense under the penal code.<sup id="cite_ref-unicef.org_126-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unicef.org-126">[126]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_speech" title="Freedom of speech">Freedom of speech</a> is addressed in the country's <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.constituteproject.org/constitution/Central_African_Republic_2013?lang=en#67">constitution</a>, but there have been incidents of government intimidation of the media.<sup id="cite_ref-2009_Human_Rights_Report_123-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2009_Human_Rights_Report-123">[123]</a></sup> A report by the <a href="/wiki/International_Research_%26_Exchanges_Board" title="International Research &amp; Exchanges Board">International Research &amp; Exchanges Board</a>'s media sustainability index noted that "the country minimally met objectives, with segments of the legal system and government opposed to a free media system".<sup id="cite_ref-2009_Human_Rights_Report_123-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2009_Human_Rights_Report-123">[123]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Approximately 68% of girls are married before they turn 18,<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup> and the United Nations' <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Index" title="Human Development Index">Human Development Index</a> ranked the country 188 out of 188 countries surveyed.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Bureau_of_International_Labor_Affairs" title="Bureau of International Labor Affairs">Bureau of International Labor Affairs</a> has also mentioned it in its last edition of the <i><a href="/wiki/List_of_Goods_Produced_by_Child_Labor_or_Forced_Labor" title="List of Goods Produced by Child Labor or Forced Labor">List of Goods Produced by Child Labor or Forced Labor</a></i>. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Central_African_Republic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Bangui_Shopping_District.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Bangui_Shopping_District.jpg/220px-Bangui_Shopping_District.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Bangui_Shopping_District.jpg/330px-Bangui_Shopping_District.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Bangui_Shopping_District.jpg/440px-Bangui_Shopping_District.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="533"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Bangui_Shopping_District.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Bangui" title="Bangui">Bangui</a> shopping district
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_the_Central_African_Republic" title="Economy of the Central African Republic">Economy of the Central African Republic</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Per_capita_income" title="Per capita income">per capita income</a> of the Republic is often listed as being approximately $400 a year, <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GNI_(PPP)_per_capita" title="List of countries by GNI (PPP) per capita">one of the lowest in the world</a>, but this figure is based mostly on reported sales of exports and largely ignores the unregistered sale of foods, locally produced <a href="/wiki/Alcoholic_beverage" class="mw-redirect" title="Alcoholic beverage">alcoholic beverages</a>, <a href="/wiki/Diamond" title="Diamond">diamonds</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ivory" title="Ivory">ivory</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bushmeat" title="Bushmeat">bushmeat</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Traditional_medicine" title="Traditional medicine">traditional medicine</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_131-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-131">[131]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The currency of the Central African Republic is the <a href="/wiki/Central_African_CFA_franc" title="Central African CFA franc">CFA franc</a>, which is accepted across the former countries of French West Africa and trades at a fixed rate to the euro. Diamonds constitute the country's most important export, accounting for 40â55% of export revenues, but it is estimated that between 30% and 50% of those produced each year leave the country clandestinely.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_131-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-131">[131]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Tree_map_export_2009_Central_African_Republic.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Tree_map_export_2009_Central_African_Republic.jpeg/220px-Tree_map_export_2009_Central_African_Republic.jpeg" decoding="async" width="220" height="172" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Tree_map_export_2009_Central_African_Republic.jpeg/330px-Tree_map_export_2009_Central_African_Republic.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Tree_map_export_2009_Central_African_Republic.jpeg/440px-Tree_map_export_2009_Central_African_Republic.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="1104" data-file-height="863"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Tree_map_export_2009_Central_African_Republic.jpeg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Graphical depiction of Central African Republic's product exports in 28 color-coded categories
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Agriculture is dominated by the cultivation and sale of food crops such as <a href="/wiki/Cassava" title="Cassava">cassava</a>, <a href="/wiki/Peanut" title="Peanut">peanuts</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maize" title="Maize">maize</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sorghum" title="Sorghum">sorghum</a>, <a href="/wiki/Millet" title="Millet">millet</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sesame" title="Sesame">sesame</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Plantain_(cooking)" class="mw-redirect" title="Plantain (cooking)">plantain</a>. The annual real GDP <a href="/wiki/Economic_growth" title="Economic growth">growth rate</a> is just above 3%. The importance of food crops over exported <a href="/wiki/Cash_crops" class="mw-redirect" title="Cash crops">cash crops</a> is indicated by the fact that the total production of cassava, the staple food of most Central Africans, ranges between 200,000 and 300,000 <a href="/wiki/Tonnes" class="mw-redirect" title="Tonnes">tonnes</a> a year, while the production of <a href="/wiki/Cotton" title="Cotton">cotton</a>, the principal exported cash crop, ranges from 25,000 to 45,000 tonnes a year. Food crops are not exported in large quantities, but still constitute the principal cash crops of the country, because Central Africans derive far more income from the periodic sale of surplus food crops than from exported cash crops such as cotton or coffee.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_131-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-131">[131]</a></sup> Much of the country is self-sufficient in food crops; however, <a href="/wiki/Livestock" title="Livestock">livestock</a> development is hindered by the presence of the <a href="/wiki/Tsetse_fly" title="Tsetse fly">tsetse fly</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Republic's primary import partner is <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a> (17.1%). Other imports come from the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> (12.3%), India (11.5%), and <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a> (8.2%). Its largest export partner is <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a> (31.2%), followed by <a href="/wiki/Burundi" title="Burundi">Burundi</a> (16.2%), <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a> (12.5%), <a href="/wiki/Cameroon" title="Cameroon">Cameroon</a> (9.6%), and <a href="/wiki/Austria" title="Austria">Austria</a> (7.8%).<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_12-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-12">[12]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The CAR is a member of the <a href="/wiki/Organization_for_the_Harmonization_of_Business_Law_in_Africa" class="mw-redirect" title="Organization for the Harmonization of Business Law in Africa">Organization for the Harmonization of Business Law in Africa</a> (OHADA). In the 2009 <a href="/wiki/World_Bank_Group" title="World Bank Group">World Bank Group</a>'s report <i>Doing Business</i>, it was ranked 183rd of 183 as regards 'ease of doing business', a <a href="/wiki/Composite_(finance)" title="Composite (finance)">composite index</a> which takes into account regulations that enhance business activity and those that restrict it.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Infrastructure">Infrastructure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Central_African_Republic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Infrastructure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">Transportation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Central_African_Republic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Transportation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Transportation_in_the_Central_African_Republic" class="mw-redirect" title="Transportation in the Central African Republic">Transportation in the Central African Republic</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Central_African_Republic_-_Trucks_in_Bangui.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Central_African_Republic_-_Trucks_in_Bangui.jpg/220px-Central_African_Republic_-_Trucks_in_Bangui.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Central_African_Republic_-_Trucks_in_Bangui.jpg/330px-Central_African_Republic_-_Trucks_in_Bangui.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Central_African_Republic_-_Trucks_in_Bangui.jpg/440px-Central_African_Republic_-_Trucks_in_Bangui.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Central_African_Republic_-_Trucks_in_Bangui.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Trucks in <a href="/wiki/Bangui" title="Bangui">Bangui</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Bangui is the transport hub of the Central African Republic. As of 1999, eight roads connected the city to other main towns in the country, <a href="/wiki/Cameroon" title="Cameroon">Cameroon</a>, Chad and <a href="/wiki/South_Sudan" title="South Sudan">South Sudan</a>; of these, only the toll roads are paved. During the rainy season from July to October, some roads are impassable.<sup id="cite_ref-e200_134-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-e200-134">[134]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>River <a href="/wiki/Ferry" title="Ferry">ferries</a> sail from the <a href="/wiki/River_port" class="mw-redirect" title="River port">river port</a> at Bangui to <a href="/wiki/Brazzaville" title="Brazzaville">Brazzaville</a> and <a href="/wiki/Zongo,_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" class="mw-redirect" title="Zongo, Democratic Republic of the Congo">Zongo</a>. The river can be navigated most of the year between Bangui and Brazzaville. From Brazzaville, goods are transported by rail to <a href="/wiki/Pointe-Noire" title="Pointe-Noire">Pointe-Noire</a>, Congo's Atlantic port.<sup id="cite_ref-Finanace_136-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Finanace-136">[136]</a></sup> The river port handles the overwhelming majority of the country's international trade and has a cargo handling capacity of 350,000 tons; it has 350 metres (1,150&nbsp;ft) length of <a href="/wiki/Wharfs" class="mw-redirect" title="Wharfs">wharfs</a> and 24,000 square metres (260,000&nbsp;sq&nbsp;ft) of warehousing space.<sup id="cite_ref-e200_134-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-e200-134">[134]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Bangui_M%27Poko_International_Airport" title="Bangui M'Poko International Airport">Bangui M'Poko International Airport</a> is Central African Republic's only international airport. As of June 2014 it had regularly scheduled direct flights to <a href="/wiki/Maya-Maya_Airport" title="Maya-Maya Airport">Brazzaville</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mohammed_V_International_Airport" title="Mohammed V International Airport">Casablanca</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cadjehoun_Airport" title="Cadjehoun Airport">Cotonou</a>, <a href="/wiki/Douala_International_Airport" title="Douala International Airport">Douala</a>, <a href="/wiki/N%27djili_Airport" title="N'djili Airport">Kinshasha</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lom%C3%A9-Tokoin_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="LomÃ©-Tokoin Airport">LomÃ©</a>, <a href="/wiki/Quatro_de_Fevereiro_Airport" title="Quatro de Fevereiro Airport">Luanda</a>, <a href="/wiki/Malabo_International_Airport" title="Malabo International Airport">Malabo</a>, <a href="/wiki/N%27Djamena_International_Airport" title="N'Djamena International Airport">N'Djamena</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paris-Charles_de_Gaulle" class="mw-redirect" title="Paris-Charles de Gaulle">Paris</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pointe_Noire_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Pointe Noire Airport">Pointe-Noire</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Yaound%C3%A9_Nsimalen_International_Airport" title="YaoundÃ© Nsimalen International Airport">YaoundÃ©</a>. </p>
      <p>Since at least 2002 there have been plans to connect Bangui by <a href="/wiki/Rail_transport" title="Rail transport">rail</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Transcameroon_Railway" class="mw-redirect" title="Transcameroon Railway">Transcameroon Railway</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Energy">Energy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Central_African_Republic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Energy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Energy_in_the_Central_African_Republic" title="Energy in the Central African Republic">Energy in the Central African Republic</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The Central African Republic primarily uses <a href="/wiki/Hydroelectricity" title="Hydroelectricity">hydroelectricity</a> as there are few other resources for energy and power.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup> The Central African Republic will likely be among the main winners after a global transition to renewable energies is completed as the country is ranked no. 7 out of 156 nations in the index of geopolitical gains and losses after energy transition (GeGaLo Index).<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Communications">Communications</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Central_African_Republic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Communications">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Communications_in_the_Central_African_Republic" class="mw-redirect" title="Communications in the Central African Republic">Communications in the Central African Republic</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Presently, the Central African Republic has active television services, radio stations, <a href="/wiki/Internet_service_providers" class="mw-redirect" title="Internet service providers">internet service providers</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Mobile_network_operator" title="Mobile network operator">mobile phone carriers</a>; <a href="/wiki/Socatel" title="Socatel">Socatel</a> is the leading provider for both internet and mobile phone access throughout the country. The primary governmental regulating bodies of telecommunications are the MinistÃ¨re des Postes and TÃ©lÃ©communications et des Nouvelles Technologies. In addition, the Central African Republic receives international support on telecommunication related operations from <a href="/wiki/ITU-D" title="ITU-D">ITU Telecommunication Development Sector (ITU-D)</a> within the <a href="/wiki/International_Telecommunication_Union" title="International Telecommunication Union">International Telecommunication Union</a> to improve infrastructure.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Central_African_Republic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:CAR_classroom.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/CAR_classroom.jpg/170px-CAR_classroom.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="255" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/CAR_classroom.jpg/255px-CAR_classroom.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/CAR_classroom.jpg/340px-CAR_classroom.jpg 2x" data-file-width="533" data-file-height="800"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:CAR_classroom.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Classroom in <a href="/wiki/Sam_Ouandja" title="Sam Ouandja">Sam Ouandja</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_the_Central_African_Republic" title="Education in the Central African Republic">Education in the Central African Republic</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Public education in the Central African Republic is free and is compulsory from ages 6 to 14.<sup id="cite_ref-ilab_141-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ilab-141">[141]</a></sup> However, approximately half of the adult population of the country is <a href="/wiki/Literacy" title="Literacy">illiterate</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Higher_education">Higher education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Central_African_Republic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Higher education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The two institutions of higher education in the Central African Republic are the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Bangui" title="University of Bangui">University of Bangui</a>, a public university located in Bangui, which includes a <a href="/wiki/Medical_school" title="Medical school">medical school</a>; and <a href="/wiki/Euclid_University" class="mw-redirect" title="Euclid University">Euclid University</a>, an international university.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Healthcare">Healthcare</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Central_African_Republic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Healthcare">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Health_in_the_Central_African_Republic" title="Health in the Central African Republic">Health in the Central African Republic</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Caf_babies.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Caf_babies.jpg/220px-Caf_babies.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Caf_babies.jpg/330px-Caf_babies.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Caf_babies.jpg/440px-Caf_babies.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="2000"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Caf_babies.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Mothers and babies aged between 0 and 5 years are lining up in a Health Post at Begoua, a district of <a href="/wiki/Bangui" title="Bangui">Bangui</a>, waiting for the two drops of the oral <a href="/wiki/Polio_vaccine" title="Polio vaccine">polio vaccine</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The largest hospitals in the country are located in the Bangui district. As a member of the <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">World Health Organization</a>, the Central African Republic receives vaccination assistance, such as a 2014 intervention for the prevention of a measles epidemic.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup> In 2007, female <a href="/wiki/Life_expectancy_at_birth" class="mw-redirect" title="Life expectancy at birth">life expectancy at birth</a> was 48.2 years and male life expectancy at birth was 45.1 years.<sup id="cite_ref-hdrstats.undp.org_146-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hdrstats.undp.org-146">[146]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Women%27s_health" title="Women's health">Women's health</a> is poor in the Central African Republic. As of 2010<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Central_African_Republic&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the country had the 4th highest <a href="/wiki/Maternal_mortality" class="mw-redirect" title="Maternal mortality">maternal mortality</a> rate in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Total_fertility_rate" title="Total fertility rate">total fertility rate</a> in 2014 was estimated at 4.46 children born/woman.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_12-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-12">[12]</a></sup> Approximately 25% of women had undergone <a href="/wiki/Female_genital_mutilation" title="Female genital mutilation">female genital mutilation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup> Many births in the country are guided by traditional birth attendants, who often have little or no formal training.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">[149]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Malaria" title="Malaria">Malaria</a> is endemic in the Central African Republic, and one of the leading causes of death.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup> According to 2009 estimates, the HIV/AIDS <a href="/wiki/Prevalence" title="Prevalence">prevalence</a> rate is about 4.7% of the adult population (ages 15â49).<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">[151]</a></sup> This is in general agreement with the 2016 <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> estimate of approximately 4%.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">[152]</a></sup> Government expenditure on health was US$20 (PPP) per person in 2006<sup id="cite_ref-hdrstats.undp.org_146-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hdrstats.undp.org-146">[146]</a></sup> and 10.9% of total government expenditure in 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-hdrstats.undp.org_146-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hdrstats.undp.org-146">[146]</a></sup> There was only around 1 physician for every 20,000 persons in 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">[153]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Central_African_Republic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r936637989">.mw-parser-output .portal{border:solid #aaa 1px;padding:0}.mw-parser-output .portal.tleft{margin:0.5em 1em 0.5em 0}.mw-parser-output .portal.tright{margin:0.5em 0 0.5em 1em}.mw-parser-output .portal>ul{display:table;box-sizing:border-box;padding:0.1em;max-width:175px;background:#f9f9f9;font-size:85%;line-height:110%;font-style:italic;font-weight:bold}.mw-parser-output .portal>ul>li{display:table-row}.mw-parser-output .portal>ul>li>span:first-child{display:table-cell;padding:0.2em;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .portal>ul>li>span:last-child{display:table-cell;padding:0.2em 0.2em 0.2em 0.3em;vertical-align:middle}</style>
      <div role="navigation" aria-label="Portals" class="noprint portal plainlist tright"> 
       <ul> 
        <li><span><img alt="flag" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Flag_of_the_Central_African_Republic.svg/32px-Flag_of_the_Central_African_Republic.svg.png" decoding="async" width="32" height="21" class="noviewer thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Flag_of_the_Central_African_Republic.svg/48px-Flag_of_the_Central_African_Republic.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Flag_of_the_Central_African_Republic.svg/64px-Flag_of_the_Central_African_Republic.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600"></span><span><a href="/wiki/Portal:Central_African_Republic" title="Portal:Central African Republic">Central African Republic portal</a></span></li>
